  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e81ea739-1638-406a-b85d-c3231cf4bfca'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer10992938664214107221"><p>"Let her prove herself worthy as a man."</p> <p> Newly knighted, Alanna of Trebond seeks adventure in the vast desert of Tortall. Captured by fierce desert dwellers, she is forced to prove herself in a duel to the death -- either she will be killed or she will be inducted into the tribe. Although she triumphs, dire challenges lie ahead. As her mythic fate would have it, Alanna so</p></span>
  <span id="freeText10992938664214107221" style="display:none"><p>"Let her prove herself worthy as a man."</p> <p> Newly knighted, Alanna of Trebond seeks adventure in the vast desert of Tortall. Captured by fierce desert dwellers, she is forced to prove herself in a duel to the death -- either she will be killed or she will be inducted into the tribe. Although she triumphs, dire challenges lie ahead. As her mythic fate would have it, Alanna soon becomes the tribe's first female shaman -- despite the desert dwellers' grave fear of the foreign woman warrior. Alanna must fight to change the ancient tribal customs of the desert tribes -- for their sake and for the sake of all Tortall.</p> <p> Alanna's journey continues...</p></span>

<div id="review_361168830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361168830" />
    <a title="Margaret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10622490-margaret"><img alt="Margaret" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341200824p2/10622490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361168830?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/10622490-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10622490-margaret?shelf=favorites-from-adolescence">favorites-from-adolescence</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361168830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1310641055637778166">I was 12 when I discovered the Song of the Lioness quartet, and they made a massive impression on me. At that point in my life it was amazing to find a series of books with such tough, relatable heroine. Alana was everything I wanted to be: strong-willed, compassionate, driven, and dead set on living on her own terms. <br/><br/>It's been a decade since I first read these books, and they still stand up pretty well. Alana still strikes me as an excellent role model for teenage girls, and she's as endearing </span>
  <span id="freeText1310641055637778166" style="display:none">I was 12 when I discovered the Song of the Lioness quartet, and they made a massive impression on me. At that point in my life it was amazing to find a series of books with such tough, relatable heroine. Alana was everything I wanted to be: strong-willed, compassionate, driven, and dead set on living on her own terms. <br /><br />It's been a decade since I first read these books, and they still stand up pretty well. Alana still strikes me as an excellent role model for teenage girls, and she's as endearing to college-aged me as she was to preteen-me.<br /><br />That being said, I have one massive problem with "The Woman who Rides Like a Man". There's an uncomfortable degree of cultural insensitivity in Alana's dealings with the Bashir (a desert tribe who adopt her). The tribe is othered to the point of Orientalism, their customs little more than a caricature of Middle Eastern culture. I was also discomfited with the fact that Alana was portrayed as a white savior, swooping in and bringing massive "moral" changes to the Bashir's traditions. It struck me as a blatant display of cultural imperialism.<br /><br />The Woman who Rides Like a Man has it's issues, but those problems can be the starting point for some great discussions. Because it raises questions about gender roles, moral relativity, and cultural issues, it could be a great selection for a teen reading group.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1310641055637778166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10000182078256878404" style="display:none">I just want to burn this book and then make myself forget about it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457711700ra/18393243.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is a synonym for horror. The whole book is like one big unfinished draft ready for its editing. The concentration of whiny-ass characters reached its maximum in this book. Alanna is the ultimate Drama Queen that can't make up her mind - does she want to have passionate sex with George or Jon? Of course, everything turns out great for her and she's a freaking hero while her brother becomes a fanatic lunatic. One of the biggest characteristics of this book is the "let's change these characters completely" or the famous "doing the 180". The plot is dull. The action is non-existent. I wanted to shoot myself during most of this miserable book. <br><br><b>Overall, this is one of those "I want to pull a Barney Stinson" kind of books again.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457720204ra/18395135.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_975507038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975507038" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975507038?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975507038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8468617733004385550">Based on what I've read on Goodreads, the general fan consensus seems to be that this book is the weakest of the quartet. I enjoyed it just as much as the previous two books, but can see why people tend to list it as their least favorite. The story takes place almost entirely in a single location, as Alanna goes to live in the desert after graduating as a knight (and killing Duke Roger) at the end of Book 2. The people she falls in with are the Bazhir, who we met briefly in Book One when she and</span>
  <span id="freeText8468617733004385550" style="display:none">Based on what I've read on Goodreads, the general fan consensus seems to be that this book is the weakest of the quartet. I enjoyed it just as much as the previous two books, but can see why people tend to list it as their least favorite. The story takes place almost entirely in a single location, as Alanna goes to live in the desert after graduating as a knight (and killing Duke Roger) at the end of Book 2. The people she falls in with are the Bazhir, who we met briefly in Book One when she and Jonathon went to the Black City, but the people and their culture is explored in much greater depth here. <br /><br />I'm not objecting to the single setting here - honestly, it was kind of nice to have the narrative slow down a little, instead of racing from one place to another and covering two years in two hundred pages - but it gave this book a very different feel than the previous two. Compared to the previous books, the pace of this one feels practically glacial, with the timeline of the whole story covering just a few months. After seeing how quickly Pierce moved through plot points in the previous books (hey, anybody remember that time we went to war with Tusaine?) I found myself wondering just how long Alanna was planning to hang out with the Bazhir. <br /><br />The majority of the book, it turns out. But to be fair, she has a lot to do. In the beginning of the story, Alanna falls in with a Bazhir tribe and they eventually accept her as one of them and then she becomes their shaman, because this is a Tamora Pierce book and Alanna of Trebond is a fucking boss at everything she does. She spends most of her time training three Bazhir kids in magic, and two of them are girls, and all of the tribespeople are like, "But a GIRL can't do magic or be a shaman!" and Alanna is like "Prepare to have your minds blown, Noble Savages!" As you can guess, the Bazhir stuff wanders into uncomfortable territory more than once. At best, they're fulfilling the Noble Savage trope and giving Alanna guidance like this is some <i>Eat Pray Love</i> white woman on a vision quest bullshit, and at worst they're just flat-out Orientalist stereotypes. There's a whole ceremony to make her an honorary Bazhir, and even though the scene itself is perfectly fine, all I could think about was that <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LzrOMXOJwjE" rel="nofollow noopener"> super racist number</a> from <i>Annie Get Your Gun</i>. The whole storyline is very much a White Savior cliche, right down to Alanna smashing her way into a culture she has almost no understanding of and insisting they change their ways immediately. The only thing that redeems this storyline is the two girls she trains as shamans - they ultimately change most of the Bazhir's views on women, so at least the people making strides to change the culture are actually <i>from</i> that culture. <br /><br />So that wasn't great. But everything else that happens here is awesome. Jonathan shows up halfway through the book and proposes to Alanna (Jonathan, honey, how many way will this not work?), and then proceeds to go full Joffrey, turning into an entitled little shit who seems to have forgotten the last eight years when Alanna was his best friend and fellow squire. They have an explosive fight where Jonathan yells at Alanna that she needs to start acting more feminine and she basically tells him to go fuck himself, and then she flounces off to go have sex with George Cooper for a while, because fuck you, Jonathan. It's glorious. <br /><br />My biggest wish for the previous book was for Alanna to make a female friend, and Tamora Pierce has answered my prayers. After two books of believing that she was the exception to the rule that girls are silly and weak, Alanna meets a goddamn plethora of women who defy that stereotype. In addition to the two Bazhir girls she trains in magic, Alanna also meets George's cousin Rispah, a female thief who was so awesome in her few scenes that I immediately started imagining her and Alanna going on a <i>Thelma and Louise</i>-style roadtrip together. She almost makes up for Delia, who you'll remember from the last book as that dumb slut who flirted with Alanna's friends and turned out to be working for Duke Roger, because girls who flirt with your boyfriends are always full of dark magic. Delia is still here, and I'm kind of hoping that she's going to be the main villain in the next book, just so she has something fun to do.<br /><br />It's not the best book in the series, but overall <i>The Woman Who Rides Like a Man</i> is another great Alanna adventure, full of excitement and magic and swordfights and sex with cute boys and fantastic conversations like this, which all little girls need to study and remember:<br /><br />"'You are a terrifying creature,' the Voice told [Alanna] solemnly. 'You do not take your place in your father's tent, letting men make your decisions. You ride as a man, you fight as a man, and you think as a man-'<br />'I think as a human being,' she retorted hotly. 'Men don't think any differently from women - they just make more noise about being able to.'<br />As Coram chuckled, Mukhtab said, 'Have you not discovered that when people, men and women, find a woman who acts intelligently, they say she acts like a man?'"</span>
  <a data-text-id="8468617733004385550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600032879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032879" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600032879?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50424456-mayim-de-vries?shelf=avoid-lifes-too-short-for-bad-books">avoid-lifes-too-short-for-bad-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600032879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16785561199029473030"><i> “Poor woman who rides like a man. You know so much, and nothing at all.”</i> <br/><br/>After the coming out, Alanna of Trebond, the sole woman knight in the realm of Tortall does <s>going</s> riding away. This is what we have been waiting for. All this arduous training and the palace shenanigans were just a prelude to what I always believed a key element in Alana’s story: fulfilling her knighthood dream. I endured the previous book only because I wanted to read about Alanna’s travels and adventures around the kingd</span>
  <span id="freeText16785561199029473030" style="display:none"><i> “Poor woman who rides like a man. You know so much, and nothing at all.”</i> <br /><br />After the coming out, Alanna of Trebond, the sole woman knight in the realm of Tortall does <s>going</s> riding away. This is what we have been waiting for. All this arduous training and the palace shenanigans were just a prelude to what I always believed a key element in Alana’s story: fulfilling her knighthood dream. I endured the previous book only because I wanted to read about Alanna’s travels and adventures around the kingdom. <br /><br />Here is what happens: <b>Alanna starts her journey, gets stuck in the first place she visits and her adventures exacerbate my previous conclusions that from a determined and hard-working girl, she grew up to be a person who expects the whole world to bend her way</b>. She comes to a people of a different culture, suffers the village-saviour syndrome, makes them adjust to her whims and lands on the top of the societal ladder which she promptly uses to challenge the Bazhir way of life (of course she knows better!). Any <b>problems she encounters, are easily resolved with the minimum of effort on her part</b>. In this regard nothing has changed from the previous book, <b>which is ludicrous because previously she was in a somewhat favourable milieu and now she is supposed to be out there, in a dangerous world</b>. <br /><br />My vacuum cleaner is more dangerous. <br /><br />Things are so terribly unpleasant for poor Alanna that when she breaks her magic toy (that was mildly exciting), instead of struggling as an ordinary human being, she gets a new toy immediately (what a letdown!). On top of this, <b>she continues her emancipation nonsense</b>. I’d be willing to ignore it even against the gender crusade fought by Alanna against the representatives of another culture, but the absolutely abysmal view on marriage (kind of a coffin you are locked in alive and buried promptly) coupled with <b>her take on romance</b>, which now, that we are firmly out of the children’s quarters and into the adult playground, <b>turned from fresh to repulsive</b>, means that I’d indeed rather spend time with my vacuum cleaner than her. <br /><br />By the way, if you hoped that the change of scenery means the end of the love triangle, all that you need to know is: the <b>love triangle is essential in this instalment</b>. All that Alanna is presently preoccupied with is <s>who to hump</s> which one of the two candidates is better. In both cases, their love and devotion is taken for granted, and <b>when pressed with need, she swaps one stud for another just waiting for it, all hot, in the starting gate</b>.<br /><br />Even the villainy in this book is not that scintillating and needs to be rehashed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[you know it’s bad if the Author is forced to bring the antagonist from the dead <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> . It means that I can basically summarise the plot line of the next book even before I have read it. <b>It would be acceptable in a children’s book, not in a novel meant for the adult audience.</b> <br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509220933?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a> ★★★☆☆<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032874?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Hand of the Goddess</a> ★☆☆☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600032895?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lioness Rampant</a> ★☆☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="16785561199029473030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1598754361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1598754361" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1598754361?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1598754361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18188313907602568811">I opened this book sailing along on a certain ship... a ship that I'd been on since book 1 ... I was convinced my feelings were never going to change! <br/><a href='http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/tumblr_me29v2JZmZ1qfsdgh_zpsbwaswot6.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459782881ra/18653517.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_me29v2JZmZ1qfsdgh_zpsbwaswot6.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>BUT THEN THINGS HAPPEN!! <br/><br/><a href='http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/anigif_optimized-27916-1428419283-5_zpstcgse7te.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459782881ra/18653518.gif' alt=' photo anigif_optimized-27916-1428419283-5_zpstcgse7te.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>And these things weren't making me happy ... NOT AT ALL HAPPY JON!! <br/><br/>And Alanna reacted just exactly how I expected she would ...<br/><br/><a href='http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/gasp_zpstdeae3dx.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

<div id="review_1804429077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804429077" />
    <a title="Sakina (aforestofbooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25145566-sakina-aforestofbooks"><img alt="Sakina (aforestofbooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597968694p2/25145566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804429077?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sakina (aforestofbooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sakina (aforestofbooks)" href="/user/show/25145566-sakina-aforestofbooks">Sakina (aforestofbooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781439115145" href="/book/show/7298451-the-woman-who-rides-like-a-man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25145566-sakina-aforestofbooks?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25145566-sakina-aforestofbooks?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25145566-sakina-aforestofbooks?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804429077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16238994106812924074">OKAY. Let's ignore my review from the past. This book made me absolutely hate Jon. I didn't like him a whole lot in the last book, but this book really goes to show how awful, conceited, and controlling he is. The second he arrives at the Bloody Hawk tribe's village, things went downhill. He's moody and annoying, taking out his anger on Alanna. He only wants to marry her to prove he can do whatever he wants. And then they have a huge argument, which I really thinks shows his true colours. Saying</span>
  <span id="freeText16238994106812924074" style="display:none">OKAY. Let's ignore my review from the past. This book made me absolutely hate Jon. I didn't like him a whole lot in the last book, but this book really goes to show how awful, conceited, and controlling he is. The second he arrives at the Bloody Hawk tribe's village, things went downhill. He's moody and annoying, taking out his anger on Alanna. He only wants to marry her to prove he can do whatever he wants. And then they have a huge argument, which I really thinks shows his true colours. Saying that Alanna isn't a real woman like the Court ladies, was honestly the last straw for me. I didn't remember much of this book from my last reread because it's always been my least favourite, but this time around I just can't stand it. I know people will argue and say that Jon is still young, but in this world, a 21 year old is a proper adult, and Jon does not act like one. <br /><br />Then we have the whole white saviour trope, with both Alanna and Jon. Alanna bringing education and freedom and women's rights to the Bazhir annoyed me so much. And she also tries to get the girls to remove their face veils because apparently that somehow limits or constricts them from becoming full-fledged shamans or sorcerers. It's eye-rolling, this whole book. Jon becomes the Voice because of course the Bazhir would want some white guy who's family has oppressed them for centuries to become their leader.<br /><br />I do remember Jon changing in the next book, but I honestly don't remember how, and I don't know if it redeems his behaviour in this one. I am glad to finally be one step closer to finishing this series and rant-tweeting on Twitter has been a great as well lol<br /><br />***<br /><br />It's amazing how your opinions change as you get older. I still love this book (and this series) as much as I did the first time around. But it's definitely eye-opening. Jon really annoyed me in this book - he has gone a bit cocky and proud because of who he is. Just like Thom! I honestly didn't quite remember much about Thom's role in this book, and realizing who he's become makes me so sad. Jon also makes me so sad, because like Alanna said, he is a good person at heart, but he's just let all this royalty and "nobleness" get to his head and has forgotten that not every woman is at his beck and call and will accept/do whatever he wants. Alanna being with him constantly kept him somewhat grounded, but I'm hoping he remembers (I think he does later on) that woman have their own rights and thoughts and opinions. And he shouldn't need Alanna constantly near him to remember that. George though...now I remember why he's so perfect for Alanna!<br /><br />(I feel kind of pressured to finish all of Tamora pierce's books before the end of the year because of the challenge, which sucks because I feel like I've rushed through this series and not drawn it out as slowly as I should have. I feel like there are so many important lessons that I should have thought over more, but I'm glad I own the book so now I can reread it as many times as I want)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16238994106812924074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loves fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/172605-kim?shelf=strongwomen">strongwomen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5882240831459740243">I love this series because it features a strong female protagonist. In fact, all of this author's work is centered around young women, which I appreciate after reading so much Harry Potter (which I love, but which lacks balance between good male and female characters, at least in the early books). Some of the other collections get repetitive, but Alanna's story stays compelling through all four books. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2389436599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389436599" />
    <a title="Olga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16609779-olga"><img alt="Olga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577911148p2/16609779.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_60932539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60932539" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/398239-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448427826p2/398239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60932539?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/398239-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60932539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16427804641035189625">In book three of the Song of the Lioness series, Alanna has just received her Knight's shield and is anxious to be off on an adventure of her own making. Accompanied by the steady Coram, who trained her as a young page, Alanna feels ready for any eventuality. Heading southward, Alanna and Coram are attacked by murderous desert dwellers and are eventually rescued by the equally enigmatic Bazhir people who offer her two options: fight one of their own warriors and join the tribe or be killed. Wise</span>
  <span id="freeText16427804641035189625" style="display:none">In book three of the Song of the Lioness series, Alanna has just received her Knight's shield and is anxious to be off on an adventure of her own making. Accompanied by the steady Coram, who trained her as a young page, Alanna feels ready for any eventuality. Heading southward, Alanna and Coram are attacked by murderous desert dwellers and are eventually rescued by the equally enigmatic Bazhir people who offer her two options: fight one of their own warriors and join the tribe or be killed. Wisely, Alanna fights and awes group with her fighting skills and compassion - except for a notable few members of the Bloody Hawk tribe. Despite all the tradition and prejudice against women, Alanna is slowing welcomed by the group, eventually becoming the tribe's newest shaman and training three youngsters to carry on her in place.<br /><br />Even though she has escaped the confines of palace life, Alanna is confronted with the reality of determining her relationship with Prince Jonathan while the ever comforting presence of George, the King of the Thieves, silently keeps watch over her. All of Alanna's friends are wonderful but George has always been a standout for me. This book finally showed a little more personality in Jonathan and, for good or bad, made for a more interesting character.<br /><br />Wherever she goes, Alanna draws attention. It's probably the whole red hair, purple eyes, warrior maiden thing she has going on but it really works for her. I'd probably stop in my tracks if she crossed my way too. That said, I love how she is constantly faced with difficult challenges where there really is no easy answer. Alanna faces each situation with maturity and intelligence that I can't help but admire. But above all, she is loyal to her friends and to the vows she made as a knight and it shows in everything she does. I am so enjoying this series and I can't wait to see what is up next for Alanna in the concluding volume, Lioness Rampant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16427804641035189625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3234857656?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beena" href="/user/show/77362575-beena">Beena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27661901-the-woman-who-rides-like-a-man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77362575-beena?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77362575-beena?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3234857656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9361147062526403327">I'm not usually one to make myself read something I'm not enjoying, but it was for a buddy read and it's not a long book (though it might as well have been a few hundred pages longer for the amount of time it took me to read it).<br/><br/>All Alanna's talked about in previous books is that she wants to be a knight and then go on "adventures". This book was meant to be her going on said adventures and turned out to be her spending nearly all her time in one place; the desert and meeting one group of people</span>
  <span id="freeText9361147062526403327" style="display:none">I'm not usually one to make myself read something I'm not enjoying, but it was for a buddy read and it's not a long book (though it might as well have been a few hundred pages longer for the amount of time it took me to read it).<br /><br />All Alanna's talked about in previous books is that she wants to be a knight and then go on "adventures". This book was meant to be her going on said adventures and turned out to be her spending nearly all her time in one place; the desert and meeting one group of people, a tribespeople; The Bazhir. The depiction of the Bazhir is really outdated and stereotyped. The main villain was killed off early which left Alanna to be the Shaman and teach her apprentices; the main part of the book was just her living in the desert and not really doing much to be honest.<br /><br />I found the way she talks and behaves <i>really</i> immature and I would've thought that Pierce would adjust her writing accordingly to Alanna's age, because it just seems like there's a child in a woman's body. Prince Jonathon being an ass came out of nowhere and didn't make any sense. Several things took place rapidly towards the end of the book but didn't seem like it served any purpose; there wasn't a coherent plot to this at all. Pretty damn boring.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9361147062526403327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_86535956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86535956" />
    <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers"><img alt="Shera (Book Whispers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446841556p2/3167178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86535956?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shera (Book Whispers)" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers">Shera (Book Whispers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=ebook-second">ebook-second</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=80s">80s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86535956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17182624998056322993">It has come up a lot in discussions about Young Adult books: How unrealistic the romance is. How it's insta-love and the girl never thinks of how the relationship will affect her. If she really loves about the guy, and what she doesn't love about him. (Oh, my! The male love interested isn't REALLY perfect.) How being with that person will affect her life and goals. Most importantly, how she wants to be treated by and because of that person.<br/><br/>I always say I've read books where it is considered and </span>
  <span id="freeText17182624998056322993" style="display:none">It has come up a lot in discussions about Young Adult books: How unrealistic the romance is. How it's insta-love and the girl never thinks of how the relationship will affect her. If she really loves about the guy, and what she doesn't love about him. (Oh, my! The male love interested isn't REALLY perfect.) How being with that person will affect her life and goals. Most importantly, how she wants to be treated by and because of that person.<br /><br />I always say I've read books where it is considered and it made for a great read. But then I could never remember the titles! Well Woman Who Rides Like a Man goes there. It shows how Alanna knows herself, well enough that she doesn't want to just rashly throw her future away for an ideal/fantasy. <br /><br />Romance isn't the entire focus by any means. Alanna is dealing with how to accept magic into her life. Becoming a teacher and a revolutionist for women. Better yet readers finally get a good look into the Bahsir. They're a fascinating people and I enjoy how change slowly comes to them. Inspired by their respect of Alanna. Alanna learns she can't take care of everyone. <br /><br />The new characters of the Bahsir are really fun to get to know and a few old favorites. There's plenty of time to flesh out other characters that are much beloved. Though unfortunately some of Alanna's Knight friends aren't here. Thom isn't getting much page time, and I think Alanna is going to be super shocked by what is transpiring. Or at least she should be! It bothers me a bit how unworried and uncaring she seems about what her brother does. I feel like because he's her brother—twin brother—there's very weird disconnect between them. I thought maybe it was because they both have issues letting people in, but they're both supposed to have loved each other immensely. There's still one more book to fix it. <br /><br />Overall I love this follow-up. Alanna is an amazing character and while her fears of the royals and palace politics are her latest fear, she's finding her own footing as the first Lady Knight in over a century. It's wonderful to see how much she's grown and that she's still fearless in her life choices. That love isn't just instant forever. People change and you never stop learning and growing. <br /><br />Oh, and the action is pretty awesome. <br /><br /><b>Sexual Content:</b> Some sex and sexual humor. This is a book written in the 80s, so it's all clean and vague on the sex scenes themselves. So no worries. <br /> <br /><b>4/5- Great! Really enjoyed it. </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://www.shera-bookwhispers.blogspot.com/2016/01/review-woman-who-rides-like-man.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Whispers</a>.</i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17182624998056322993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=magic-time-travel">magic-time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=love-triangle-of-doom">love-triangle-of-doom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=slump-buster">slump-buster</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1480710642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18372301538382760041">Each book is better than the last, and that's saying a lot considering how much I've enjoyed each previous book. I like the decisions Alanna's made up to this point, but most especially as of the end of this book, though I think she should probably check in on that brother of hers…<br/><br/>Can't wait to start the final book, though I'm already wishing it didn't have to end. ;0)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2546495508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2546495508" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8263750-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587266605p2/8263750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2546495508?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/8263750-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2546495508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14609550871762576003">This book didn't have the adventure that the other two novels had, but it was still very enjoyable for me. Throughout this, Alanna continues to grow up. She's strong and fights for what she wants (or doesn't want) like she always has, but what got me throughout this one is that we see Alanna really learning to accept more of who she is. Since she ends up being a shaman, she has to focus on another part of herself that she had previous kinda tucked away and never wanted to deal with which forces </span>
  <span id="freeText14609550871762576003" style="display:none">This book didn't have the adventure that the other two novels had, but it was still very enjoyable for me. Throughout this, Alanna continues to grow up. She's strong and fights for what she wants (or doesn't want) like she always has, but what got me throughout this one is that we see Alanna really learning to accept more of who she is. Since she ends up being a shaman, she has to focus on another part of herself that she had previous kinda tucked away and never wanted to deal with which forces her to bring it back out. It was nice to see that expansion of you can be more than one thing. Since this really is directed at a younger audience, I thought that was an incredibly good message. There were also others throughout it that would involve spoilers, so I won't mention them. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1518598694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1518598694" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1518598694?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=project-nostalgia">project-nostalgia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1518598694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6413558197386301948">As an aside, I read this on the plane, too, on my must-be-3+-years-old Nook Glowlight. If I'm tied into the B&N ecosystem, there's really no newer ereader option, is there? I heard that the black refresh doesn't appear on newer ereaders, but I've also read a few downer articles about the future of the Barnes and Noble ebook platform, and I'm a little worried. <br/><br/>Onto the book! I only have two highlighted notes, so I'll mention those and then talk about my general impressions of the book.<br/><br/>First, I di</span>
  <span id="freeText6413558197386301948" style="display:none">As an aside, I read this on the plane, too, on my must-be-3+-years-old Nook Glowlight. If I'm tied into the B&amp;N ecosystem, there's really no newer ereader option, is there? I heard that the black refresh doesn't appear on newer ereaders, but I've also read a few downer articles about the future of the Barnes and Noble ebook platform, and I'm a little worried. <br /><br />Onto the book! I only have two highlighted notes, so I'll mention those and then talk about my general impressions of the book.<br /><br />First, I did not like this: "A skinny man wearing the green robes of a Bazhir shaman, or petty wizard, threw back his hood. His scraggly beard thrust forward on a sallow chin." Yeahhhhh. He must be evil because he's sallow and can't grow much of a beard! Appearance dovetailing with character is my <i>least</i> favorite means of description. Plus: a petty wizard? And here I thought shamans were exactly like mages, only Bazhir! The rest of the book only does its absolute best to convey that impression.<br /><br />Second, I really, really liked the entire section where Jonathan discussed becoming the Voice. I thought it was unlikely, though I did like that the magic of the ceremony means all the Bazhir know exactly what to expect from Jonathan and how he'll do. At least there's that. Otherwise, isn't it a little insulting to invite a non-Bazhir outsider to become the final voice on their court systems and questions of history and tradition? What I did really like: the way Jonathan talks about becoming the Voice, as something that will be vital to his future kingship, highlights something so interesting about this series - there's a very traditional medieval perception of honor and duty. These are nobles who reach for power, because it's their currency and ultimately their obligation to their families, but also have an eye toward its responsibilities. They're not careless or stingy or power-mad. It's what makes them such good heroes, that they <i>are</i> very clearly of their world, even as they represent the best of it. <br /><br />I'm also fascinated with the idea that Jonathan's restlessness is cured by the acceptance of this tremendous responsibility. That more than anything is a sign he's going to be a great king. Showing, not telling! HURRAH.<br /><br />It's odd that the Voice ceremony feels more - I don't know - difficult? Real? - than the Ordeal descriptions. Maybe it's because Jonathan has to slice his own arm open. Maybe because there's so clearly a heavy aura of magic, while the Ordeal just feels like a series of nightmares.<br /><br />I also really liked the evolution of Amman Kemail. Here's someone who doesn't abuse the system to challenge Jon initially, but who really has valid concerns. And then he's gracious in defeat <i>and</i> wise enough to recognize that Jon "will do" as the Voice. I LIKED HIM. I hope he sends his kids to Corus to become knights. <br /><br />SPEAKING OF, remember the Bazhir in the Kel books? Isn't knighthood training only for nobles? The Bazhir don't seem to have a traditional feudal structure, so who exactly qualifies, and why?<br /><br />What I also like about Jon in this book: how peremptory he is! Sure, it's frustrating for Alanna, incredibly so - and it's not the easiest to read about, either - but here's a guy who's a prince and knows he's going to be king one day. Having him be Mr. Nice Guy wouldn't quite ring true. Plus, I love it when Alanna shouts at him.<br /><br />Alanna fascinates me in this book. Not just because she made up the most randomly phrased spells, and they worked (how much magical theory has she ever learned? Not much) but because she not only forces the tribe to accept her, but to accept her students, and her position is so matter-of-fact. I don't know how she thought she'd be successful at that, especially since she really doesn't know much about their history.<br /><br />You know, I remembered this book as the desert book. I didn't remember how much it sets up <i>Lioness Rampant.</i> Thom particularly - and Claw - and Josiane, I suppose, though she's so tertiary she's almost unnecessary. Which, confession time, is my favorite book of this series. CAN'T WAIT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6413558197386301948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=young-adult-n-kids">young-adult-n-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=library-borrow">library-borrow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=hear-me-roar-and-gender">hear-me-roar-and-gender</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631944311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8974466222795763036">Oh, this series.<br/><br/>In this installment, Alanna has become a knight and goes off to the desert where she spends some time with the Bazhir culture, and a whole lot of whiteness happens to them. For those of us who were all "But these are all white characters!" during the first couple of books, rest assured because there are some not-as-white people here, and there called the Bazhir. Well, they show up a bit in the last book, but here we get to learn about their culture in more detail. Alanna is there</span>
  <span id="freeText8974466222795763036" style="display:none">Oh, this series.<br /><br />In this installment, Alanna has become a knight and goes off to the desert where she spends some time with the Bazhir culture, and a whole lot of whiteness happens to them. For those of us who were all "But these are all white characters!" during the first couple of books, rest assured because there are some not-as-white people here, and there called the Bazhir. Well, they show up a bit in the last book, but here we get to learn about their culture in more detail. Alanna is there and meets some new people and actually makes friends! They aren't all in love with her like a lot of her previous friends have been, but there's a mutual respect.<br /><br />And so Alanna then teaches them a bunch of stuff they don't know and becomes their shaman and teaches them about the ways of the world. Basically, she's doing missionary work. And it's just as unsettling to read about as any true missionary work is.<br /><br />As far as adventuring goes, this is sort of the extent of it. Alanna doesn't go off into wild flights of fancy, and essentially stays with the Bazhir throughout the story which is unlike the first two books when she'd throw down for any little thing, and I think a lot of readers disliked that about this book. I thought it was fine, but you know, I'm not as invested in these stories as some readers are.<br /><br />In other Alanna-news, she is well-versed in the ways of the sexual world by this book. She and Jonathan are hot and heavy through most of the story until he's all "Can't you be more like a lady? I like ladies" which of course is basically another way of saying "You're so much prettier when you smile." Yeah, fuck you, Jonathan. I don't care if you <i>are</i> a prince. Shut your trap.<br /><br />But there's still that George guy waiting in the wings, so for those of you who have been wanting <i>that</i> to happen, rest assured again!<br /><br />Shamans and sex. That's pretty much this story.<br /><br />I'm not a big fan of the title here. Alanna is called "the woman who rides like a man" a lot, and that's supposed to be a good thing, but it's annoying, like hearing "you run like a girl" or "you throw like a girl." It's not helpful at all. I get that Alanna was blowing the Bazhir's mind by showing them all the things girls can do that are just like the things boys can do, but it's still an unfortunate title all around. <i>The Woman Who Rides Like a Woman</i> would be confusing, but also would have a better message, if you're just going by the title and not reading the book (which happens more than you think since kids are growing up reading titles on a bookshelf, trying to find one that appeals to them).<br /><br />Anyhow, Alanna is still amazing at everything (sex included), and now I am just about to begin the fourth book to see what kind of shenanigans Alanna gets into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8974466222795763036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78004691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18275220383319218615">[first read: 3 January 2008]<br/><br/>Alanna, knighted and revealed, heads south to begin her stint as a wandering knight, eager to forget the unrest at court over her deception and also her slaying of the King's cousin in combat. In her first year as a knight, she joins and instills change upon the desert-dwelling Bazhir; witnesses Prince Jonathan become the Voice; swaps one Royal lover for another; and begins to understand herself as Alanna instead of Alan. <br/><br/>1. Still don't like Jonathan. NOT SORRY. (Alth</span>
  <span id="freeText18275220383319218615" style="display:none">[first read: 3 January 2008]<br /><br />Alanna, knighted and revealed, heads south to begin her stint as a wandering knight, eager to forget the unrest at court over her deception and also her slaying of the King's cousin in combat. In her first year as a knight, she joins and instills change upon the desert-dwelling Bazhir; witnesses Prince Jonathan become the Voice; swaps one Royal lover for another; and begins to understand herself as Alanna instead of Alan. <br /><br />1. Still don't like Jonathan. NOT SORRY. (Although, I must acknowledge that this is an interesting and realistic situation to place your heroine in: Alanna is in love with an unsuitable man. How the situation solves itself--some yelling before the parties separate indefinitely--is also realistic but definitely not fulfilling.)<br /><br />2. I HATE that George feels like a rebound in this. Absolutely the text tries to make it not so, bit I'm sorry, it all screams REBOUND--especially because Alanna invites him to bed IMMEDIATELY after finding out that Jonathan had moved on to another woman. LKJDFKJ <br /><br />3. I guess the gist of my feelings is this: I like Alanna and her adventures. I like the world. I like this lady knight struggling to find her place and how to use her voice in a world that has no place and no ear for her. I <i>like</i> all of that. <br /><br />I hate the romance so much though that I could throw things! I hate that Alanna has so little agency! I hate that Pierce has problematic approaches to gender and race! <br /><br />4. Is it important that George gets a chapter from his POV? OF COURSE IT IS. <br /><br />5. THOM WTF (Part of me rebels against Thom's looming fall because his story--one of isolation and pride and idiocy--is one I feel rather keenly (especially as a isolated prideful idiot myself?). As much as I adore Alanna's fumbling connections and heart, part of me wonders what Thom's story would look like. (Not that we need another asshole boy-sorcerer story, but.)<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9072137150629412308">It feels like the series increases in its juvenile sensibility. Maybe it’s because Alanna’s youthfulness made sense when she was a tween, and now that she’s an adult her relative lack of maturity (and the author’s lack of maturity in her writing) seems jarring and not as it should be. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Also…so she whines when he’s too ardent in his affections, she whines when he’s willing to treat her as just a friend.   <span id="freeText9072137150629412308" style="display:none">It feels like the series increases in its juvenile sensibility. Maybe it’s because Alanna’s youthfulness made sense when she was a tween, and now that she’s an adult her relative lack of maturity (and the author’s lack of maturity in her writing) seems jarring and not as it should be. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also…so she whines when he’s too ardent in his affections, she whines when he’s willing to treat her as just a friend. Ugh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I’m also annoyed about how the main characters are made to be almost constantly perfect, with their only occasional pointed-out flaws being acting like annoying a-holes. I would like to see them be more like humans. And maybe for Alanna to not have everything always turning out great for her, with things consistently turning out badly for anyone who might dare to not worship her. Like her apprentice pointing out that it’s unfair how she has like a million Super Magical Items is a sign of his being a fool? So if readers might feel the same way, clearly they’re being foolish.<br /><br />Not sure what happened to the feisty, fascinating protagonist of the first book (by the second, she’d already gone partway into a boy-obsessed perfect snowflake who had things land in her lap just to make the story Cooler rather than her earning them through merit shown on her part…but only partway).</span>

<div id="review_2112978421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2112978421" />
    <a title="Linaria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7357268-linaria"><img alt="Linaria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581382547p2/7357268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2112978421?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linaria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linaria" href="/user/show/7357268-linaria">Linaria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357268-linaria?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357268-linaria?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112978421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10764329024962897422"><a href='http://www.waywardreviews.blog' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530969820i/25937678.png' alt='waywardreviews.blog' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This book is my least favorite of the Alanna quadrilogy. It's still a solid book, especially in the context that this book was so important for teenage girls when it came out.<br/><br/>This book is basically Alanna off to have adventures. The book starts strong, with a fight between her and some desert bandits. Eventually she ends up spending time with the tribe and joining them. The majority of the plot of this book is really set up for the next book, but it's interesting to see the changes that time</span>
  <span id="freeText10764329024962897422" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.waywardreviews.blog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530969820i/25937678.png" alt="waywardreviews.blog" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This book is my least favorite of the Alanna quadrilogy. It's still a solid book, especially in the context that this book was so important for teenage girls when it came out.<br><br>This book is basically Alanna off to have adventures. The book starts strong, with a fight between her and some desert bandits. Eventually she ends up spending time with the tribe and joining them. The majority of the plot of this book is really set up for the next book, but it's interesting to see the changes that time has had on Alanna, Jon and George. The three of them do a bit of growing, and their relationships change as a result. To be honest, at the end of the book, there is still a lot of growing for some of them to do *cough* Jon *cough*<br><br>I do like that Alanna stays strong to wanting to be a knight and not wanting the kind of life that Jon does. The two of them, though they care for each other, have different priorities. It's a sad, but necessary realization that they make, in terms of their future. This does lead to Alanna spending more time with George, of which I do whole-heartedly approve.<br><br>Again, this was a strong book, especially when it first came out. While I am looking through this through nostalgia glasses a bit, I think that it still passably stands on it's own now. It's also a perfect setup for whats to come in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10764329024962897422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3161644769" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out"><img alt="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473475487p2/16915869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3161644769?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out">Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780739349519" href="/book/show/6764192-the-woman-who-rides-like-a-man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=animals-pets">animals-pets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3161644769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer890119333895642862">3.5 stars<br/><br/>From a purely story structure standpoint, this is a slight improvement on the previous book. The writing for these first three Tortall books has been solid, no doubt. The narrative flows, the characters are well-developed and the arcs for the story and the characters never feel like they're being driven by the author, at least not too much. <br/><br/>Alanna, newly knighted and ready for adventure, heads out with her trusty man-of-arms Coram and heads south to see where the road might take her. So</span>
  <span id="freeText890119333895642862" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />From a purely story structure standpoint, this is a slight improvement on the previous book. The writing for these first three Tortall books has been solid, no doubt. The narrative flows, the characters are well-developed and the arcs for the story and the characters never feel like they're being driven by the author, at least not too much. <br /><br />Alanna, newly knighted and ready for adventure, heads out with her trusty man-of-arms Coram and heads south to see where the road might take her. Soon enough, they're being ambushed by hill people and kind of rescued/kind of not by the Bazhir, a tribal people who have long been in conflict with Tortall. Alanna comes to them at a time of change, or more accurately brings the change with her, and not everyone is pleased by these turns of events.<br /><br />Alanna continues to skirt the Mary Sue tropes, accomplishing impossible feats with near ease and befriending everyone around her except the unreasonable fanatics, aka the bad guys, but I like that she's exploring her feminine side more. It's all well and good to rebel against traditional gender roles - lord knows I hate those things myself - but it's often at the expense of women who embrace those roles, making them lesser than the mannish heroine. Alanna here learns to respect those traditions and those women while still maintaining her own sense of self. <br /><br />The Bahzir are an interesting culture and while Alanna and Jonathan have an unfortunate bit of White Savior trope around them, I like that it too isn't at the expense of the Bazhir peoples and that it's acknowledged that Tortall isn't exactly progressive either. There are positives and negatives with both cultures, so the text is able to sidestep some of the more problematic elements that might have otherwise bogged this down. The Bazhir can and do accept change based on their own standards and it's good that text calls Alanna out when she's being unreasonable in what she thinks they should or shouldn't do. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though making Jonathan the Voice of the Tribes was a bit too much, imo. I understand the reasoning behind it, but surely it would've been better to choice a Voice who lives amongst the tribes and would be willing to bridge the alliance with Tortall that they so desperately need. I'm not sure how Jonathan will accomplish splitting his duties and loyalties to two separate people once he's the crowned king. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The love triangle is painfully dull, but it was never a trope I liked to begin with. I do like that Alanna insists on having relationships on her own terms, and that she realizes that loving someone isn't necessarily enough when it comes to marriage. All that said, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[between overtly sexist Jonathan who just assumes that of course Alanna will want to be his princess/queen, and the rogue thief George who accepts Alanna in all her aspects both mannish and feminine, I know which one I'd choose. And I love that Alanna - for now - chose neither. She's not finished becoming herself yet, and still wants to have adventures. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The text did kind of meander once they left the Bazhir and spends the last couple of chapters setting up final book in this quartet. There's much ado in the capital with Alanna's twin brother Thom, which is handled in a very not subtle way and doesn't leave any mystery about where the next book is going to be heading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="890119333895642862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
